# Completing the Know Your Partner (KYP) form

- Business structure.
- Full legal name as it appears on the business registration document (if the name that’s prefilled in the KYP form is incorrect, you can indicate this in the form and you’ll be directed to update your Accommodation Agreement with the correct name).
- Business registration number (if applicable).
- Name of trade register your business is registered in (if applicable).
- Registered business address (not the address of your property).
- Tax Identification Number (TIN) and issuing country
- VAT number and issuing country.
- Public contact info that's displayed on your property listings.

Depending on whether you use our payment solutions, you might also be asked to provide additional information specifically for Booking Holdings Financial Services (BHFS) in the KYP form. This information includes, but isn’t limited to:

- Details of the individual(s) who owns 25% or more of the total shares, voting rights, or other equity of the business entity (i.e. ultimate beneficial owners).
- Details of the individuals who manage and run the company (i.e. directors).

We’ll need to verify at least one person who manages or directs your business. The individuals you've identified as directors in the Know Your Partner (KYP) form will be asked to submit the following information:

- Proof of identity – depending on your location, this is usually a government ID, driver's license, or passport.
- Proof of address – this document needs to have been issued within the last six months. It can be a utility bill, credit card statement, or bank statement. You’ll need to provide the full document, but you can block out sensitive information such as utility costs, bank account numbers, balances, and transactions.

If you enabled Payments by Booking.com with bank transfer payouts, you’ll need to provide your bank account details to comply with regulatory requirements and to receive payouts for your reservations.

Here’s how to add or edit bank details:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click the
**Finance**menu, then Finance settings. - Under
**Receiving payouts from Booking.com**, click**Edit bank details**to update your information. - Click Save.

If you manage multiple properties, be sure to check the **Bank details** page through the **Finance **menu in the group Extranet.

## FAQs

-
If you’ve already completed the KYP form but are still receiving reminders, it could be because your properties are listed under multiple legal entities, each with its own Legal Entity ID number. Each legal entity is required to have its own KYP form. Submit the remaining forms for any other entities, or use your primary account to update your portfolio by moving all properties to a single legal entity.

-

-
If your property is still active on our site, we’re required to ask you to complete the KYP form even if you haven’t added any availability.

If you want to remove your property or end your partnership with us, you can follow the steps in this article.

# Understanding eligibility and opting in and out of Payments by Booking.com

Payments by Booking.com is a service that facilitates guest payments for you according to your preferred policy. Depending on your property’s payment settings, you’ll receive payouts by bank transfer or virtual credit card.

## What's on this page:

**Checking if you're eligible or already active on Payments by Booking.com**

To find out if your property is active or eligible for Payments by Booking.com, sign in to the Extranet and click **Finance** to see the drop-down menu**.**

- If the
**Payout information**or**Virtual cards management**option appears in the menu (and the**Payments by Booking.com**option doesn’t appear), it means you’re already active on Payments by Booking.com. Click it to learn more. - If the
**Payments by Booking.com**option appears, you’re eligible for the service but it’s not yet active. To activate it, click**Payments by Booking.com**, then**Sign up**. - If neither the
**Payout information**,**Virtual cards management**, nor**Payments by Booking.com**options appear in the drop-down menu, your property isn’t eligible for this service.

**Learning more about ineligibility for Payments by Booking.com**

If you aren’t eligible for Payments by Booking.com, you can reach out to us for more info by following these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet
- Click
**Inbox**, then**Booking.com Messages** - In the sidebar, click
**Compose a new message** - Select the topic
**Receiving my payouts**, then the subtopic**How do I join or leave Payments by Booking.com?**

You can also find more info about our payment products on the Partner Hub.

**Managing payments if you’re not eligible for Payments by Booking.com**

If your property isn’t eligible for Payments by Booking.com, you’ll need to manage your guests' payments yourself:

- If you accept credit cards, you can either charge your guest before or upon arrival/departure, depending on their reservation policy.
- If you don’t accept credit cards, your guest can pay upon arrival or departure in your local currency. If you want to charge a prepayment or damage deposit, you’ll need to contact the guest to decide on a payment deadline and arrange it yourself.

Learn more about how to set your payment preferences.

**Opting out of Payments by Booking.com**

You can opt out of Payments by Booking.com by following these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Finance**, then**Finance settings**. - Click
**Payments by Booking.com status**,select**Deactivate Payments by Booking.com**, and follow the steps to proceed with deactivation. - Click
**Deactivate payments to**confirm your changes.

Once you’ve deactivated Payments by Booking.com, you’ll have to pay the commission proactively at the end of the month. Learn more about commission payments here.

If you still have pending payouts, you can decide to receive them via bank transfer or virtual card. If you choose the bank transfer option, you’ll receive your pending payouts as gross bank transfer payouts, not net payouts. You can view your remaining bank transfer payouts on the Extranet’s **Payout information** page by doing the following:

- Sign in to the Extranet
- Click the
**Finance**menu - Click
**Payout info**

# Payments by Booking.com: FAQs

In this article, you’ll find answers to the most frequently asked questions about Payments by Booking.com, including information about virtual credit cards (VCCs) and bank transfers. Note that not all payment solutions are available in all countries or for all property types. We share rolling updates whenever these become available.

You can see which payment method we’ll use for each booking under the Price column on the Extranet’s Reservations page. You can also see the details of the payment method in the Payment details section of the Reservation details page for each booking.

This FAQ is for partners using Payments by Booking.com. For information about payments that are not facilitated by us, check this general payments FAQ.

**Key takeaways**

- Payments by Booking.com facilitates your guest payments, then pays you via bank transfer or virtual credit card (VCC).
- A VCC is a temporary digital Mastercard linked to an existing credit card.
- If you’re paid by VCC, we’ll send you a new VCC for every relevant booking.
- If you’re paid by bank transfer, then you’ll be paid in daily, weekly, or monthly installments.

## What's on this page:

You need to provide your guests with an invoice when they check out. This is because the reservation agreement is a direct transaction between you and your guest, not with Booking.com. You can provide the invoice on paper, by email, or both.

Here’s some more important information about invoices:

- We hold no responsibility for invoicing, and we don’t send invoices for any reservation to you or your guest.
- Make sure you issue invoices in your guest’s name, or another name you’ve agreed with them.
- For payouts you receive by VCC, the cardholder name will always be
**Booking.com (Agent).** - When we charge a guest, there may be tax implications for you. To learn more about local taxes, take a look at this article.
- You can export your invoices to use for tax declarations or other record keeping purposes.

For more information about invoices, take a look at this article.

When a guest uses a Booking Sponsored Benefit, we’ll cover a portion of the price so that the guest pays less. However, you should still provide them with an invoice for the full price. If a guest needs the documentation for tax or reimbursement purposes, then they should submit the receipt from you and the booking confirmation from us, which indicates the discount.

-
If you decide to refund a guest and we haven’t paid you for the reservation, we just won’t transfer the payout to you. Instead of paying you, we’ll refund the guest on your behalf.

If we’ve already paid you for the booking by bank transfer, we’ll deduct the amount we refund the guest from your next payout via bank transfer. If you’re not due to receive a payout at that time, you’ll need to pay us the amount we refunded to the guest. We’ll send you a debit note to let you know about this.

If we’ve already paid you for the booking using a virtual credit card—and you’ve already charged the VCC—you’ll need to refund it. To learn more about refunding VCCs, take a look at this article. If you haven’t charged the virtual credit card yet, you don’t need to do anything.

Yes, all properties using Payments by Booking.com can be booked with Wallet Credits. If your property doesn’t use Payments by Booking.com, you’ll need to opt in to be booked with Wallet Credits.

## Getting paid by virtual credit card (VCC)

-
A virtual credit card (VCC) is a temporary digital Mastercard linked to an existing credit card. It functions like a regular credit card and helps guests make secure online payments.

Here’s what you need to know about charging VCCs:

- For every relevant booking you receive, we’ll send you a new VCC.
- As long as each VCC stays active, you can charge it as many times as you like until the balance reaches zero.
- Each VCC has an activation date that's determined by whether the booking is refundable or not.

Find more info on VCCs here.

-
Here’s how to charge a VCC for a reservation that the guest paid for online:

- Sign in to the Extranet and click the
**Reservations**menu - Click the guest’s name or reservation number to view the
**Reservation details**page - Click
**View credit card details** - Enter the VCC details using your Point of Sale (POS) machine
- Charge the available
amount displayed

For a more detailed explanation of how to charge VCCs, watch this tutorial. If you use a channel manager or property management system (PMS), learn more about charging VCCs in this article.

- Sign in to the Extranet and click the
-
If something goes wrong when you try to charge a virtual credit card (VCC), you’ll be able to see the reason on the

**Reservations details**page about 30 minutes later. You can find some of the most common issues with charging VCCs in this article. -
If you receive a cancellation, no-show, or modification and are owed money, we’ll send you an email with updated virtual credit card (VCC) details.

-
If you’ve already charged a virtual credit card (VCC), there are two situations when you may need to refund it:

- You or your guest cancel or modify a booking or the guest doesn’t show up, and you agree to waive any fees that would apply.
- A reservation is canceled due to Force Majeure. In these cases, guests shouldn’t be charged for stays they can’t make and we waive commission on the affected reservations.

In both cases, we’ll refund the guest, and you’ll need to refund the same VCC you originally charged. To learn how to do this, take a look at this article.

-
When a guest makes a booking and pays for it online, we’ll send you a virtual credit card (VCC) along with the booking details. This card gives you access to the exact amount for that booking, and you can charge the virtual card as you would any credit card. Just make sure you do this after it's activated.

-
If you meet the following criteria, you can charge VCCs as soon as the reservation becomes non-refundable:

- You’ve paid your invoices on time for the last 12 months, according to the payment due dates
- You’ve been working with us for at least six months and have validated guest stays and reviews

We'll notify you by email if you qualify to charge your virtual credit cards before check-in.

We’ll review whether or not you meet these criteria every four months and will email you if anything changes.If you don’t meet the criteria during our review, then you can charge the VCCs one day after check-in, or at check-in for US properties. -
We’ll send you an email once a VCC is activated. You’ll have 365 days after the check-out date to charge the VCC. After that, the funds will belong to us because they’ll be considered financial breakage (i.e. revenue from services that were paid for but not used).

We’ll email you a weekly summary showing VCCs from check-outs in the last week with open balances. This isn’t a cumulative report on all uncharged VCCs – only about the previous week’s. You’ll be able to see the transaction details on the Extranet for 547 days (18 months) after the check-out date.

-
If you’re asked to enter a zip code when charging a virtual credit card (VCC), you can use the guest’s or your own zip code.

-
Your payment service provider will generally charge a fee between 2% and 3% for facilitating each transaction. The exact amount you’re charged may depend on local laws and any additional fees your bank may charge. For more information, contact your payment service provider.

-
Exchange rates don’t affect your payments if you've set the price of your rooms in the same currency you use to charge virtual credit cards (VCC).

If you receive a VCC in one currency but charge it in another, Mastercard will convert the amount using its own exchange rate. You can find out what this is on the Mastercard website.

-
You’ll pay commission for these bookings the same way as other bookings. Each payment you receive by virtual credit card (VCC) will be for the total gross amount of the booking. When we email you the VCC details, we’ll include a breakdown of the amount you’ve been paid. We’ll also invoice you separately for your commission fees.

-
If you’re eligible, here’s how you can switch from Virtual Credit Card to Bank Transfer:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Finance**, then**Finance settings.** - Click
**Payout method**and**edit payout method,**then follow the steps to proceed with the switch.

We currently only offer the option to switch from virtual credit card to bank transfer. We’re still working on introducing the switch from bank transfer to virtual credit card. If the option isn’t available on the Extranet, you can’t switch payout methods.

When you request a payout method switch, it will take five days to process. New reservations during that period will be moved to bank transfer – you’ll be informed through the Extranet if the switch fails.


## Getting paid by bank transfer

-
Find out if you’re eligible here.

-
This depends on the payment schedule you've set up and your bank. It can take a few days before the payment reaches your account.

**If you’re set up for monthly payments,**we’ll process payments by the 15th day of the month after the guest checks out.**If you’re set up for weekly payments,**we’ll process payments every Thursday for reservations where the guest checked out during the previous week, which runs from Thursday until Wednesday. If the Thursday when we'd usually process your payment is a public holiday, we’ll process it on the next business day.**If you’re set up for daily payments**, we’ll process payments one day after check-out. We don’t process payments on weekends and public holidays. Note: At the moment, the possibility to have daily payments is limited to select countries. We’re working toward expanding this feature to more countries.

To check or change your payment schedule, sign in to the Extranet, click on the

**Finance**menu, and select**Finance settings**and then**Payout timing**to select your preferred payout schedule. -
Here’s how to download your commission invoices:

- Sign in to the Extranet
- Go to
**Finance****,**then**Invoices** - Choose the year you want to filter by
- Click on “Download PDF” under the number of the invoice you want to download

To see the reservations included in each invoice, click

**View statement**under the invoice amount.Every month, we’ll also email you payout documents with details of reservations that guests paid for online, plus any refunds. To download these payout documents:

- Sign in to the Extranet
- Go to
**Finance****,**then**Payout information** - Click on the arrow next to the period you’re interested in seeing a list of reservations for
- Click
**PDF**or**CSV**to download the payout document

-
Depending on the country you’re in and payment model you’re using, your payment will either be gross or net.

If you receive a gross payout, we’ll pay you the total amount of your reservations. We’ll then invoice you for commission normally. Your commission invoice will include all bookings from the previous period, including any bookings that weren’t paid for online.

If you receive a net payout, we’ll pay you the total amount of your reservations minus the total amount of all your invoices. You won’t have to pay commission separately.

-
Here’s how to change the bank details we use to pay you:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Go to the
**Finance**menuand then click on**Finance settings**. - Under
**Receiving payouts from Booking.com**, click**Add bank details**or**Edit bank details**. - Enter your new bank details.
- Click “Update bank details.”

It can take up to five business days for your bank details to update in our system. If you change your bank details again while they’re updating, the update time resets back to five days.

Once the bank details are updated and confirmed, the next payout will be sent to your bank account according to your selected payout timing – daily, weekly, or monthly. To learn more about updating your bank details, watch this tutorial.

-
To list a property on Payments by Booking.com with a foreign bank account, you can’t accept credit card payments and have your property listed in a country that belongs to the Single Euro Payments Area (SEPA). For countries outside of SEPA, the bank account has to be located in the same country as the property is listed.

-
Exchange rates don’t affect your payments if you set the price of your rooms in the same currency as we make your bank transfer payment in. If the currency you set your rooms in isn’t the same as the one we make your bank transfer payment in, we’ll convert the amount using the rate of a third-party service provider the day before we send your remittance advice.

If we make your bank transfer payment in a different currency from the one of your bank account, your bank will convert the amount using their own exchange rate. To find out what this is, contact your bank directly.

To find out which currency we’ll make your bank transfer payment in, check the payout document we email you each month. To download these payout documents, follow these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet
- Go to
**Finance****,**then**Payout information** - Click on the arrow next to the period you’re interested in seeing a list of reservations for
- Click
**PDF**or**CSV**to download the payout document

-
The total amount shown on your invoice only includes amounts we charge commission on, such as room rates. The total reservation amount on your remittance advice is the total amount we’ve collected from guests on your behalf. This includes room or unit rates plus any additional fees, unless they’ve been broken down per person and you’ve set them as

**excluded**on the Extranet. We don’t charge you commission for these excluded fees. -
If the amount of your commission invoice is higher than the amount we pay you by bank transfer, we’ll collect the difference from your bank account. We need you to set up Direct Debit to allow us to do this unless Direct Debits aren’t available in your country.

To learn more about paying your commission invoice by Direct Debit, check out this article.

-
Depending on your property’s location and settings, we only offer the option to switch from Virtual credit card to Bank transfer at this point (see VCC section). We’re working on introducing the switch from Bank transfer to Virtual credit card – we’ll inform you when it becomes available in your market.


## Stripe facilitated bank transfers

-
Stripe is a payment service provider for businesses that enables secure and efficient payment processing. It’s currently available for some partners in the US and Canada. Find more information in our payments FAQ for property management companies in the US and Canada.

We use the location details and other items from your property information to auto-generate a property description with the most relevant info for potential guests. If your address changes, it’s important we know as soon as possible.


**In this article**


**Updating your property address**

If your address has changed and isn’t the one you provided when the registering with Booking.com, it’s important we know as soon as possible. This helps us avoid showing incorrect information on your property page and in your guests’ booking confirmation details.

You can change your address by sending us a message. Here’s how:

- Log in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Inbox**, then **Booking.com messages**. - Click
**See contact options**. - Choose
**Property** **details** as the topic and **Other** as the subtopic. - Click
**See all contact options **or** Compose new message**. - In the
**Message** field, enter the new correct address and the reason for the change. - To verify that your new address is accurate, under
**Attachment** click **Browse** or **Choose file** and attach a copy of a recent utility bill that shows the new address. This can be a recent bill for gas, electricity, water, sewage, phone, or taxes. - Click
**Send message**.

Once we receive your request, we’ll review it and update your address in our system. We’ll provide you an update on your request within five business days.


**Updating your location and changing your position on the map**

If your location on the map doesn’t correspond with the address location on Booking.com, you can update it by following these steps:

- Log in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Inbox**, then **Booking.com messages**. - Click
**See contact options **or **Compose new message**. - Choose
**Property** **details** as the topic and **Adjust your location on the map** as the subtopic. - Click
**Update map location**. - In the map that opens, click and drag the red pin to where you want your property to show up on the map.
- Click
**Save new location**, then **Done**.

Once we receive your request, we’ll review it and update your address in our system. We’ll update the distances mentioned in your property information within 48 hours.


**Getting property map coordinates from Google Maps**

We ask for your property’s map coordinates so your location is displayed correctly on Booking.com. This also affects distances to local landmarks and places of interest, so it’s important that you enter accurate coordinates for your property.

To get your property’s coordinates, follow these steps:

# Contacting us for support

We’re always here to help and answer any questions, urgent or not. If you're experiencing a **non-urgent **or** finance-related issue**, we recommend contacting us via the Extranet inbox. If you have an **urgent question**, give us a call.

In this article, you can find all the ways to contact us.

Try to look for an answer to your question on Partner Help.

We don’t have an email address, but you can message us via the Extranet inbox. We’ll do our best to get back to you within **two days**, but sometimes it may take a little longer. To help us assist you faster, please include:

- As much detail as possible about the issue you're facing or your question.
- What solutions you’ve attempted so far, if any.

If you’re having trouble accessing your Extranet account, check out these tips for signing in to your account.

Follow these steps to send us a message:
If you have more than one account, you can access the inbox of each of your properties from your primary account’s
We show up to 50 properties at a time on the Group homepage, so you might need to go through multiple pages if your portfolio is larger. |


Note: The Extranet inbox might not be available if you haven’t completed registration. If so, complete your registration to access your inbox.


### Message topics

When sending us an Extranet message, make sure you select the right topic. Here’s a short explanation for each topic:

**Rates & Availability**– loading or adjusting rates and availability, prices, and room policies.**Promotions**– setting up a deal or promotional rate.**Reservations**– bookings, cancellations, requesting arrival time, changes to bookings, payment.**Opportunities**– sales and growth opportunities in the Opportunity Center.**Guest reviews**– specific comments from a guest, responding to a review, Guest Review Score.**Invoices and commission**– any finance-related questions, payment confirmation, dispute an invoice, reopen a property, VAT and local taxes, direct debits.**Receiving my payouts**– payout info, charging guests’ virtual credit cards, Payments by Booking.com, or providing bank account details.**Analytics**– how your property is performing on our platform.**Property details**– extra charges, photos, room details, policies, changing a property name, adjusting your location, and changing your property description.**Account**– changing your password, updating your contact details, devices, channel manager, or terminating your contract.

Sign in with your Extranet credentials to see our full list of contact numbers. If you’re having trouble accessing your Extranet account, check out these tips for signing in.

You can message us via the Pulse app. Here’s how:

- Sign in to the
**Pulse app**. - Tap
**More**. - Tap
**Help**. - Select the envelope symbol.
- Select the relevant topics and subtopics.
- If no topics are relevant, select any topic and subtopic, then select
**Still need help? See all contact options**. - Tap
**Message**and compose your message. - Tap
**Send message**.

# Changing your property description or room details

Your property page description is automatically generated based on the information you provide on the Extranet. When you correct or change your facilities, room details, or location on the Extranet, the corresponding information in your property page description updates automatically.

## What's on this page:

**How the property description is generated**

We use your facilities, location details, and other items from your property info to auto-generate a property description containing the most relevant information for potential guests. This description appears under the photos on your property page.

We’re always working to optimize these descriptions. We keep them relevant by always offering new options to add, like mentioning more facilities and services, improving location information, or adjusting priorities as users’ needs evolve.

Auto-generated content is highly effective at attracting potential guests, provided best practices for creating and updating property descriptions are followed:

- We’ve done extensive research for various segments of travelers to understand what they most want to read in a property description.
- We use guest behavior data on our website to determine the length, style, and structure of our descriptions. For example, we know guests spend an average of less than one minute reading property descriptions, so our auto-generated descriptions are short.
- We’re focused on optimizing for search engines, so people can discover your property faster when they search for accommodations. We don’t copy/paste or duplicate text because this affects search engine optimization (SEO) and may make your property harder to find online.
- Auto-generated descriptions are available in 36 languages and are updated in real time. Descriptions in some languages aren’t direct translations of the English description, so there may be some discrepancies between languages. We’re working on automating description generation in another 11 languages in the foreseeable future.
- We use a unified tone of voice and language across all descriptions to help users find the information they’re looking for faster and choose the right property for them.

**Use the ****fine print section** to add any other information about your property that guests must know before booking, and that can’t be shared elsewhere on the property page. For legal reasons, we can’t include any mandatory costs, taxes, deposit information, or cancellation/payment policies in the fine print.

**Keeping your information up to date**

Since we use information you provide on the Extranet, it’s important that your facilities, location details, and room information is up to date. Make sure you add all facilities and amenities available at your property to give the most comprehensive description. You can learn more in our Updating your property page and host profile article.

**Correcting info in your description**

The goal of auto-generated property descriptions is to make sure they’re easy for guests to find and understand, and that your information is always up to date as you make changes to your rooms, facilities, and location.

We don’t change these auto-generated descriptions unless there’s a factual discrepancy. If something is incorrect regarding the property type, facilities, or location information you’ve provided, here’s how you can fix it:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Property**, then**View your descriptions**. - For changes to your property description, click
**Spotted a typo? Request a fix**and describe the fix you need in the text field that appears. - For changes to your
room description(s), click**Request a correction**below the room you’d like to update, then describe the fix you need in the text field that appears. - Click
**Request a fix**.

Our content team will revise your requested changes and advise on the next steps.

Note: It isn’t possible for you to manually adjust the number of years mentioned in the part of the auto-generated description that says “Has been welcoming guests since [date].”

**Updating your facilities and services**

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Property**, then**Facilities & services**. - Update the facilities and services available at your property.
- Click
**Save**.

**You can update your facilities and services on the go using Pulse.**

**Updating your room amenities**

It’s important guests know what to expect when they arrive at your property. If the information about amenities available at your property isn’t up to date, here’s how to change it:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Property**, then**Room amenities**. - For each room amenity, check or uncheck the box to show whether it applies to
**all rooms**or just**some rooms**. You’ll then be able to specify which rooms it applies to. - Click
**Save**.

**Updating your location and changing position on the map**

Property location features in the description, so it's important that the geographical location is correct. If your property’s location appears to be inaccurate and you’d like to change the geographical coordinates we display on our platform, follow these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Inbox**, then**Booking.com messages**. - Click
**See contact options**. - Choose
**Property****details**as the topic and**Adjust your location on the map**as the subtopic. - Click
**Update map location**. - In the map that opens, click and drag the red pin to where you want your property to show up on the map.
- Click
**Save new location**, then**Done**.

We’ll update the distances mentioned in your property information within 48 hours.

Keep in mind that your property’s location on the map needs to accurately reflect where it is actually located based on your address. If you move the red pin too far, we’ll suggest updating your property’s address to make sure it’s correct. Moving the pin also affects distances to local landmarks and places of interest.

Read more about changing your property’s location.

**Changing your property layout and room or unit details**

You can change other property details like property layout and room type based on maximum occupancy by following these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Property**, then**Property layout**or**Room details**. - Click
**Edit**. - Change information such as room type, room name, location, bed options, occupancy, and bathroom details.
- Click
**Continue**.

You can edit room names to create custom names for personal reference on the Extranet, but only you can see your custom names there – travelers don’t see these on our platform.

You can also customize the names of your rooms or units, change the room or unit type, and adjust maximum occupancy for individual rooms or units. Finally, it’s a good idea to add room facilities. This gives potential guests a clear idea of what they can expect at your property.


**Adding property facilities**

You can list the facilities available at your property to better manage guest expectations. On the Extranet’s **Facilities and services** page, you’ll find **Top facilities** – those that guests search for the most. If you don’t see a specific facility on the Extranet, we suggest either selecting a closely related one or adding the information to **About the property**. You’ll find this on the Extranet by clicking **Property**, then **Your profile**. Read more about updating your facilities.


**Your property description**

We use your facilities, location details, and other information from your property page to auto-generate descriptions that contain the most relevant information. These descriptions are automatically generated in multiple languages and appear under your photos on your property page.

Auto-generated content is highly effective at attracting guests because it’s:

**Always up to date** – Auto-generating the description means it’s guaranteed to be an up-to-date reflection of the facilities you’ve chosen on the Extranet. **Attention-grabbing** – Our data shows that guests don’t read the whole description. With auto-generated content, our descriptions are short and concise, and they contain only the key traveler information.**Easily discoverable online** – With SEO-optimized, auto-generated content, your property is more easily found in search results.**Instantly available in 25 languages** – We market your property all around the world in at least 25 supported languages, updated in real-time. Descriptions in some languages aren’t direct translations of the English description, so some discrepancies are possible. **Accurate** – Our data shows that the information in auto-generated descriptions is more accurate than in manually written descriptions.

We don’t change these auto-generated descriptions unless there’s a factual inaccuracy. If you find incorrect information, you can follow these instructions to change your property description.


**Adding photos**

Our data shows that guests typically stay only ten seconds on a page before leaving. Photos are the most engaging form of content, and the best way to boost bookings is by showing how unique your property is.

You’ll need to upload at least one photo of your property to sign up for our platform, but we recommend adding as many as possible. You can always add, change, or delete them later. Read more about which photos you need for a home, apartment, or vacation rental and what photos attract families.


**Updating your profile**

You can update your profile by adding personalized information – these are the things that make you, your property, and your neighborhood unique.

Completing your profile tells guests more about yourself and what makes your place special. It paints a complete picture of your property and shows potential guests that you’re an authentic person.

Descriptions should be personable yet professional, so make sure to include relevant information about yourself and your property as well as the surrounding area. You can even write a welcome message for future guests. You can update the information via the Extranet or the Pulse app by following the steps below.

# Setting up length of stay and advance reservation restrictions

Setting up length of stay and advance reservation restrictions can give you more control over your bookings. They prevent travelers from booking a stay that’s shorter or longer than you’d like, or with too much or too little notice.

You can add, change, or remove restrictions via your Extranet calendar or using the Pulse app.

**In this article**

**Understanding length of stay and advance reservation restrictions**

These restrictions determine how travelers can book a stay at your property, based on your preferences. If you apply these restrictions, potential guests can only make a reservation with you when their search criteria match the conditions you’ve set.

Minimum length of stay restrictions determine the minimum number of nights guests can book at your property. Minimum advance reservation restrictions determine how far before the check-in date a guest can book a stay with you.

You can apply a minimum length of stay restriction of up to 31 nights. For example, if you set a minimum length of stay restriction of three nights, your property won’t appear in the search results of travelers looking for two- or one-night stays.

You can also set up length of stay restrictions that only apply to bookings with specific check-in dates. These are known as minimum length of stay from arrival restrictions.

You can set minimum and/or maximum advance reservations for specific rooms or properties on specific dates. Our system counts backwards from midnight on the check-in date, which means you can set restrictions both in terms of days (D) as well as hours (H) before check-in. For example:

- If you want guests to book at least one day before check-in, the minimum advance reservation time is one day. You would then enter 1D in our system.
- If you want to allow same-day bookings until 6 pm, the minimum advance reservation time is six hours (counting backwards from midnight). You would then enter 6H in our system.
- If you want guests to book at least three days and five hours in advance, the minimum advance reservation time is three days. You would enter 3D5H in our system.
- If you don’t want guests to book more than ten days in advance, the maximum advance reservation time is ten days. You would then enter 10D in our system.

Once you set your reservation restrictions, your property will only appear in search results when guests’ search dates match these restrictions. The more restrictions you set, the fewer potential guests will see your property. Learn more about all restrictions


In the following sections, we describe the possible ways to set restrictions, depending on which Extranet calendar view you use.

**Managing restrictions using the List view calendar**

If you’re using the List view** **calendar, here’s how to apply and edit restrictions to your rooms and rates:

- Log in to the Extranet
- Click
**Rates and Availability**or**Calendar and Pricing**, then**Calendar**. - Click the
**Restrictions**checkbox next to the date selector at the top of your Calendar page, or find the room you’d like to set up the restriction for, then click the drop-down arrow next to the room rate to see all your restrictions. - On the restriction rows, select the date you’d like to make changes to. To select multiple dates, drag the blue rectangle over all the dates you want to restrict. You can also click
**Bulk edit**to change restrictions for multiple dates. - Click the
**Activate**button, then**Save.**

When using the list view calendar, you can set the following length of stay and advance reservation restrictions:

**Minimum length of stay**– 2 to 31 nights. However, you can increase this by changing your default length of stay limit, which is 30 nights. You can do this on the Extranet by clicking**Property**and selecting**Policies**. Select**30+ night stays (monthly stays)**, click**Edit**, and indicate whether you accept bookings up to 45, 60, 75, or 90 nights.**Maximum length of stay**– 1 to 30 nights. You can increase this by following the same steps as for minimum length of stay.**Minimum advance reservation**– 1 hour to 360 days.**Maximum advance reservation**– 1 hour to 360 days.

**Managing restrictions using the Monthly view calendar**

When you’re using your calendar in Monthly view, you can only set up a Minimum advance reservation and Minimum length of stay. To set up a Maximum advance reservation and length of stay, you’ll have to switch to List view.

If you prefer the monthly view** **calendar, here’s how to apply and edit restrictions to your rooms and rates:

- Log in to the Extranet
- Click
**Rates and Availability**or**Calendar and Pricing,**then**Calendar**. - Click the drop-down menu on the right-hand side of the page and select Monthly view.
- Select the date you want to change. To select multiple dates, drag the blue rectangle over all the dates you want to restrict.
- In the panel on the right side of the page, find the applicable rate and click
**Restrictions.** - Choose how many nights you’d like your
**Minimum stay length**to be and your**Minimum advance reservation**time. - To remove minimum stay restrictions, select
**1 night**in the same menu. - Click
**Save**when you’re done.

When using the monthly view calendar, you can set the following length of stay and advance reservation restrictions:

**Minimum length of stay**– 1 to 7 nights**Minimum advance reservation**– 4 hours to 7 days

Monthly view calendar is only available to partners who don’t work with a connectivity provider. Those who do can still manage rates and availability—including restrictions—via their provider’s interface. Learn more about connectivity providers in this article.

**Managing restrictions using rate plans**

If you're using rate plans, here's how to apply and edit restrictions to your existing rate plans. The changes will be applied to all open days.

- Log in to the Extranet
- Click
**Rates and Availability**or**Calendar and Pricing**, then Rate plans. - Choose the rate plan you prefer to change.
- In the plan preview, you’ll be able to see the current restrictions.
- Click Edit to be guided to the selected rate plan page.
- Click Edit next to the
**Minimum stay**to manage the length of stay, or**Bookable**to set up how many days in advance your guests can make a booking. - Click
**Save**when done editing the restrictions. - Click
**Apply changes**when you’re done.

**Managing restrictions using Pulse**

You can also manage Minimum advance reservation and Minimum length restrictions using the Pulse app.

Here's how for a **single** date:

- Open the Pulse app and tap
**Availability**. - Tap the property you’d like to manage, if you have more than one.
- If you’re viewing the dates in a calendar, choose the room type you’d like to manage by tapping its calendar and selecting the date. If you’re viewing the dates in a list, scroll down to the date you want to edit and tap the room type.
- Tap the minimum length of stay and choose the number of nights you want to apply restrictions to.
- Under
**Minimum advance reservation**, adjust the minimum number of nights or hours, working back from midnight. - Tap
**Save**on iOS or the**checkmark**on Android to save.

Here’s how to apply and edit **Minimum advance reservation** to your rooms and rates for **multiple** dates:

- Open the Pulse app and tap
**Availability**. - Tap the property you’d like to manage, if you have more than one.
- If you’re viewing the dates in a calendar, choose the room type you’d like to manage by tapping its calendar and selecting the date. If you’re viewing the dates in a list, scroll down to the date you want to edit and tap the room type.
- Tap
**Edit multiple dates**and select the date range you want to make changes to. - Tap
**Rates and restrictions**. - Tap the minimum length of stay and enter the number of nights you want to apply restrictions to.
- Under
**Minimum advance reservation**, adjust the minimum number of nights or hours, working back from midnight. - Tap Save on iOS or the checkmark on Android to save.

# Updating your rates and availability

You can increase your visibility in search results and attract early bookers by loading rates and availability well in advance. You can update your rates and availability via your calendar on the Extranet, either in the list or monthly view. Be sure to load prices for any dates you’ve opened, so potential guests can see and book those rooms or units. Travelers can book up to 16 months in advance.

Reminder – your rates may not be displayed in the currency of your choice. The currency is set up on the Extranet as a default option and can’t be switched because of internal processes related to payments and billings.

## What's on this page:

**Managing your availability**

Watch this video to learn how to easily manage your property’s availability using the Extranet calendar:

**Updating your rates and availability in list view**

If you're viewing your calendar in list view, follow these steps to update your rates and availability:

- Log in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Rates & Availability**and then on**Calendar**. - Find the room or unit type you’d like to update availability for, then adjust how many of them you want to sell and on which dates in the
**Rooms to sell**row. - You can then edit the price for that room type in the
**Rate plan**row. **To make changes for multiple days at once**, click a cell and drag the blue slider across all the dates you want to apply the change to. Add the number of rooms or units and the price per night in the pop-up box that appears, then click**Save**.**To make changes for more than one month at once**, click**Bulk edit**for the room or unit type you want to update. In the panel that appears, select how many rooms or units you’d like to sell on which dates and for what price, then click**Save changes**.**To make changes for multiple room or unit types at once**, click**Bulk edit**, then select**Multiple room types**when the panel appears. Adjust the number of rooms or units to sell for the ones you want to update, then click**Save changes**.

Note: It may take a few minutes to see your availability refreshed on the platform. If you’re working with a connectivity provider, factor in possible delays from the provider.

If you work with a connectivity provider, you may not be able to use the Bulk edit option in the Extranet calendar view. In some instances, if you’re using a PMS or channel manager, you might be able to use the Bulk edit function, but your connectivity provider will override calendar changes the next time it syncs. Use your connectivity provider’s software to update your property’s availability on our platform. Read this article to learn how to manage your availability through your connectivity provider.

**Updating your rates and availability in monthly view**

If you're viewing your calendar in monthly view, follow these steps to update your rates and availability: Keep in mind that the monthly view isn’t always available to partners using a channel manager.

- Log in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Rates & Availability**and then on**Calendar**. - In the drop-down menu, select the room or unit you’d like to update.
- Select the date or date range that you’d like to update by clicking and dragging the slider in the calendar, or by selecting the
**Start date**and**End date**in the panel. Click the**Advanced date selection**drop-down if you’d like to specify which weekdays you’d like the changes to apply to. - In the panel, specify the number of rooms or units you’d like to sell for that room or unit type, which Rate Plans apply, how much you’ll charge, and whether it’s non-refundable (this option is available to properties that only have one Rate Plan). You can also add or adjust restrictions to your Rate Plans here.
- To be available for travelers to book, make sure the days you’re applying the rates to also have rooms or units marked
**Open**for bookings. - Scroll down and click
**Save**to apply the changes.

Note: It may take a few minutes to see your availability refreshed on the platform.

**Checking if your property is open and bookable**

You can check the Extranet calendar to see when your property is available to book and when it isn’t. You can also see this info on the Pulse app. Different colors indicate the status of your rooms or units:

**Green**–your room or unit is open and available to book on that date**Red**– your room or unit isn’t available to book on that date

There are several reasons for a room or unit not being available to book. You’ll see one of these reasons in the red badge under the name of the room or unit in your list view calendar:

**Closed**– you closed this room or unit. If using Pulse, you can make it open and bookable again by switching the toggle to the right. To do this on the Extranet calendar, click the**Rooms to sell**row – the room should automatically turn from red to green.**No inventory**– you haven’t added any inventory to your rooms or units yet or you’ve reduced your inventory to**0**. To make it open and bookable again, add inventory.**Price missing**– you haven’t added a price to your Rate Plan. To make your room or unit open and bookable again, add at least one price to a Rate Plan attached to this room or unit.**Rate closed**– your Rate Plans for that date are closed. To make your room or unit open and bookable again, open at least one Rate Plan that’s attached to this room or unit.**Multiple blockers**– a combination of issues is preventing your room or unit from being bookable. Click the**Rooms to sell**row to see exactly which issues need to be addressed.**Sold out**– the rooms or units you’re selling on our platform have all been booked for that date. If you have more availability and want to become open and bookable again, add availability to a room or unit.**Fully booked**– all your rooms or units have been booked for that date (this only applies to the Pulse app).

If your property doesn’t appear on the search page, make sure your rooms and units:

- Were added to your inventory
- Are open for bookings
- Have open rate plans set up
- Have a price added to each rate plan

Remember – to specify how much you want to charge for reservations, you need to add the price in your Extranet calendar for each date and room type in the **Rate plan** row.

It’s also possible that the restrictions you’ve set are affecting your property’s visibility on our platform. For example, when you only accept bookings for a minimum number of nights, your property won’t appear in search results for fewer nights than your set minimum. Also, if your minimum length of stay restriction is higher than the number of consecutive days you have available, you won’t appear in the search results.

# Everything you need to know about virtual credit cards

Learn how to charge a guest's credit card

Virtual credit cards (VCCs) are temporary digital Mastercards we use to pay out partners through Payments by Booking.com. They work like regular credit cards and guarantee payouts when you’re owed money. You don’t need to pre-authorize or validate them, which can save time.

## What's on this page:

## How virtual credit cards work

**How virtual credit cards work**

VCC is one of the payout methods we use to pay partners who use our Payments by Booking.com service. If guests pay online, they can do so using their preferred payment method. We then load that payment onto a VCC that you can charge like a regular credit card with a point of sale (POS) system. A point of sale (POS) system that accepts VCCs is required for this payout method.

Here’s how you can find out if your property is eligible to join Payments by Booking.com with a VCC payout method:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click the
**Finance**menu - Click
**Payments by Booking.com**

A few things to keep in mind about how we’ll send you payments from VCCs, how to charge them, and how long they remain valid:

- We’ll send you a new VCC for every new booking you receive that’s payable via Payments by Booking.com. Each VCC has a unique card number, expiration date, and CVC.
- Every new VCC you receive will be activated according to the reservation policy. For non-refundable bookings, this is the same date as the booking date. For all other reservations, you can charge the VCC when the reservation becomes at least 90% non-refundable. If you’re a new property or don’t follow these criteria, you’ll be able to charge the VCC one day after check-in (at check-in for partners in the US).

Here's how you can see which reservations have been paid for and which have an active VCC:

- On the
**Virtual cards management**page, you'll find details on all VCCs that still need to be charged or refunded. - Based on the activation date, you can enter the VCC details in your POS system and charge the VCC as you would any other credit card to receive your payment.
- All VCCs need to be charged within 12 months of the guest check-out date. After this point, the card will become inactive and we won’t reissue a new VCC for the reservation.
- We’ll send you reminder emails after the check-out date if you haven't charged the card yet.
- You can charge a VCC multiple times until the balance reaches zero.

We don’t charge any fees for partners on Payments by Booking.com using VCC as a payout method. However, your payment service provider may charge you a fee for using a VCC. Read more about how much Payments by Booking.com costs.


**Charging virtual credit cards**

To charge a VCC, follow these steps:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click
**Reservations**. - Click the guest’s name or reservation number.
- Click
**View credit card details**. - Enter the VCC’s details using your POS system.
- Charge the full balance available in your VCC. The available balance can be found in the VCC details, reservation details, or in
**Virtual cards management**.

You can also see all your available VCCs by clicking **Finance** and selecting **Virtual cards management**. Keep in mind that you’ll need to be signed in with admin access or an account with Reservations access rights to see the card details.

If you use a property management system or channel manager, you can find your VCC under each reservation’s payment details. If you don't see this information, contact your connectivity provider for further assistance.


**What to do if you’re having trouble charging a virtual credit card**

Here are the most common issues with charging VCCs and what to do to resolve them:

POS error messages:

**“Do not honor/the VAN can’t be authorized prior to activation date”**– Check the activation date on the Extranet’s**Reservations**page to make sure the card is already active.**“Do not honor/insufficient funds”**– Check that the amount you’re charging isn't higher than the VCC balance and try again. Keep in mind that certain fees and taxes may be excluded from the price. These fees are typically set on a per-person basis. In that case, you'll need to collect them directly from the guest during their stay. You can see the amount available on the VCC and the charge breakdown for each booking on the**Reservations**page.**“Do not honor/invalid CVC or expiration date”**– Check that the CVC code and expiration date you entered are correct.**“Invalid merchant”**– If your POS machine merchant code is invalid, contact your payment service provider for help. You can only charge VCCs if you’re a merchant registered as an accommodation provider, but you can change your code if necessary.

VCC operations errors:

**Security lock**– You’ve had too many failed charge attempts in a short period of time. Try again in 24 to 48 hours.**Using the same currency to charge the VCC as the currency used to load the VCC**– Using a different currency doesn’t necessarily mean you can’t charge a VCC, but it can lead to two potential issues:**Partial charges**– You might end up charging less than the amount available on the card, meaning funds may remain on the card. Always make sure your card has no money left.**Insufficient funds error**– Attempting to charge more than the available balance on the VCC can result in an “insufficient funds” error.

**Don’t pre-authorize the VCC**– If you have, you should either settle the authorized amount with the provided authorization code or cancel the authorization and charge it again.**Enter your, your guest’s, or our zip code**– If you’re asked to enter a zip code when you charge the VCC, you can use the guest’s, your own, or ours (1011 DL).**Make sure your POS machine supports charging virtual cards**– Contact your payment service provider for assistance. They might be able to offer you a different POS that supports online charging service.**Your card has a zero balance**– Make sure your card is already active to be charged. If the card is active but displays “zero,” it can be due to the few seconds/minutes a card needs to be loaded. If you’re seeing a “zero” balance, your provider may not have updated the system with the amount that was loaded onto the card. You can check the amount to charge on the Extranet.**Incorrect amount**– If you charged the card, you can refund the amount and charge again.

All our virtual cards are valid, so there’s no need to test-authorize them. If you’re not seeing the VCC details, it’s because the card isn’t active yet.

If you’re still having trouble charging the VCC, contact us via the Extranet inbox. Learn more about charging VCCs in our tutorial.


**How virtual credit cards work with cancellations, no-shows, and modifications**

If you’re owed money because a reservation was canceled, modified, or the guest was a no-show, you’ll be able to charge the VCC as per the reservation policy.

Depending on the cancellation date, you can charge the VCC as follows:

- If cancellation happened before April 18, 2024, you can charge a cancellation fee on the supposed check-in date.
- If cancellation takes place after April 18, 2024, you can charge a cancellation fee as soon as the reservation is canceled.

If you agreed to waive the applicable fees for the cancellation, modification, or no-show but have already charged the VCC, you'll need to refund the same VCC. You can do this even if the card has expired – just enter the current month as the expiration date instead. Learn more about refunding VCCs.


**How to deactivate virtual credit card payments**

Here’s how to deactivate VCC payments if your property is based in the EEA, the UK, or Switzerland:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click the
**Finance**menu - Click
**Finance help**to check if there’s an option to switch from VCC to bank transfer payout. If so, there’s no need to opt out of Payments by Booking.com – you can start getting paid via bank transfer.

If your property is based outside of the EEA, the UK, or Switzerland and you want to disable VCC payments, you need to opt out of Payments by Booking.com since we don't offer the option to switch from VCC to bank transfer in your region. Here’s how:

- Sign in to the Extranet.
- Click the
**Finance**menu - Click
**Finance settings**.

Under **Payments by Booking.com**, click **Deactivate Payments by Booking.com**.
